### Post by oldos2er on 2013-05-01
Have you looked at the log?

---

### Post by bcbc on 2013-05-01
If Wubi is trying to download an ISO, it means it doesn't like the one you've got. The logfile should indicate what the problem is as oldos2er mentioned. 

Note that if you try to navigate manually to the log file, parts of the path are hidden by default in Windows so you need to unhide them first. But you can directly go to the directory by using the path variable %TEMP%, or open the logfile in notepad with the full path:

Press Windows key, R(un), and enter:
```
notepad [COLOR=#000000]C:\Users\KASC\AppData\Local\Temp\wubi-13.04-rev279.log[/COLOR]
```

or (the same):
```
notepad %TEMP%\[COLOR=#000000]wubi-13.04-rev279.log[/COLOR]
```

---

---

### Post by bcbc on 2013-05-02
You need to run wubi with the --32bit option if you want to force a 32 bit install, because your computer architecture is 64bit, but the ISO you've supplied is a 32bit ISO - and due to the different kernel used for 64bit and 32bit, Wubi is rejecting the local 32bit iso. This is a bug since they introduced differently named kernels for the 64bit vs 32bit ISOs.

tl;dr 
the Workaround is to supply --32bit to force Wubi to use the local 32bit ISO. You can either run Wubi from a command prompt (CMD.EXE) as follows:
```
wubi.exe --32bit
```

Or create a shortcut as described here: [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/WubiGuide#Can_I_force_Wubi_to_download_and_install_a_32_bit_version_of_Ubuntu.3F](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/WubiGuide#Can_I_force_Wubi_to_download_and_install_a_32_bit_version_of_Ubuntu.3F)

---
